  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fe8567bb-a4a8-42a7-a273-92e076c7a3fa'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer11143610843383731645">Andie had it all planned out. When you are a politician’s daughter who’s pretty much raised yourself, you learn everything can be planned or spun, or both. Especially your future. Important internship? Check. Amazing friends?   <span id="freeText11143610843383731645" style="display:none">Andie had it all planned out. When you are a politician’s daughter who’s pretty much raised yourself, you learn everything can be planned or spun, or both. Especially your future. Important internship? Check. Amazing friends? Check. Guys? Check (as long as we’re talking no more than three weeks).<br /><br />But that was before the scandal. Before having to be in the same house with her dad. Before walking an insane number of dogs. That was before Clark and those few months that might change her whole life. Because here’s the thing—if everything’s planned out, you can never find the unexpected. And where’s the fun in that?</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1513839961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1513839961" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1513839961?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1513839961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15266210201134820279"><i>“If whole galaxies could change, so could I. ”</i><br/><br/>It’s seriously impossible for me not to fall in love with the summer season while reading a Matson book. <b>The Unexpected Everything</b> was exactly what I was looking for right now.<br/>It is the ultimate summer read, filled with hilarious, thrilling, and poignant characters that I won’t be forgetting anytime soon.<br/><br/>I thought I wasn’t going to enjoy this one as much as her last book because of the length, but Morgan Matson really knows how to make the pages fly </span>
  <span id="freeText15266210201134820279" style="display:none"><i>“If whole galaxies could change, so could I. ”</i><br><br>It’s seriously impossible for me not to fall in love with the summer season while reading a Matson book. <b>The Unexpected Everything</b> was exactly what I was looking for right now.<br>It is the ultimate summer read, filled with hilarious, thrilling, and poignant characters that I won’t be forgetting anytime soon.<br><br>I thought I wasn’t going to enjoy this one as much as her last book because of the length, but Morgan Matson really knows how to make the pages fly by. Her pacing in books makes it completely unputdownable— She perfectly captures that feeling during those magical summer nights where time seemed to stop. Seriously, hours passed in what felt like seconds while reading this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462532946ra/19009112.gif" width="256" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462532946ra/19009113.gif" width="256" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462532946ra/19009114.gif" width="256" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains *spoilers*.<br><br>The story all starts with a conference in front of Andie’s house, she’s the only daughter of a prominent congressman, who’s suddenly caught up in a scandal that threatens to upend not only his career but the next national election.<br><br>When you are a politician’s daughter who’s pretty much raised yourself, you learn everything can be planned or spun, or both. Especially your future.<br>But that was before the scandal. Before having to be in the same house with her dad. Before walking an insane number of dogs. That was before Clark and those few months that might change her whole life.<br><br>After the conference, Andie plans to leave home for the summer to participate in her pre-med (pre-pre-med-med) program, until an unfortunate phone call informs her that her perfect summer isn’t going to play out just as she’d planned.<br><br>Andie not willing to give up on her plans for a great summer yet, starts anew with a mysterious dog-walking job. Which I absolutely adored, especially when she met her boss, Maya, for the first time. I was smiling so much. So I just had to then spent some time on <a href="http://bookspoils.tumblr.com%20" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> looking at cute dogs. And I’m still amazed with how utterly beautiful these pictures are:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462532946i/19009115.jpg" width="320" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462532946i/19009116.jpg" width="320" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462532946i/19009117.jpg" width="320" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://handsomedogs.com/post/142352619694/amber-bailey-skagit-valley-tulip-festival" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a><br><br>While doing said dog-walking job, she meets Clark. And he turns out to be a lot more than Andie was expecting. Their meet-cute was hilarious with the whole Bertie the dog situation.<br><br>I also really liked Clark’s initial nervousness around Andie, especially when he tried to ask her out:<br><i>“I was just . . . trying to get a sense of your schedule.” He blinked, like he’d just heard himself, and I could see the tops of his ears were starting to turn red. “Wow, that sounded creepy. I didn’t mean that in, like, a weird way. I think I’m making this worse. Oh god.” He took a breath, then swallowed hard. “I was wondering, you know, what you do. At night.” He stared at me in horror after he said it, like he couldn’t quite believe the words had come out of his mouth. “Oh, man,” he muttered, closing his eyes behind his glasses for a moment. “This isn’t going well.”<br>I had to bite my lip to stop myself from smiling wide.”</i><br>Me too, Andie, me too…<br><br>Oh, and when her dad and Clark met I was laughing so hard and feeling just as baffled about Clark’s life.<br><br><i>“Dad, this is Clark Goetz-Hoffman,” I said, just as Clark said, “McCallister.”<br>“What?” I turned to look at him.<br>“Clark McCallister,” Clark said.<br>“I thought your last name was Goetz-Hoffman.”<br>“You two need a minute to confer?” my dad asked, looking between the two of us.”</i><br>Clark wrote <b>the book</b>, he wrote the book, he wrote the book—throughout <b>The Unexpected Everything</b> we got little snippets of another story called A Murder of Crows written by a certain C. B. McCallister.<br>And I was pretty impressed with him when I connected the dots. (Also, I’m really glad it was explained early on in the book and not dragged out.)<br><br><i>“I blinked at him, trying to figure this out. I had assumed Clark was my age, or close to it, though I was now starting to question everything. Because people who were my age, or close to it, didn’t write bestselling fantasy books. They didn’t have movies based on their books with huge movie stars in them. How was this even possible?<br>“I published the first one when I was fourteen,” Clark said, clearly reading the confusion on both our faces. He gave an embarrassed shrug. “Homeschooled kids have a lot of time on their hands.”</i><br><br>And even though their actual first date was really awkward, I’m glad it went that way because no insta-love.<br><i>“But it was too bad, I realized, as I looked at his profile, lit up by his dashboard light. He was really, really cute. And he seemed nice. But apparently, somehow, that wasn’t always enough. (I made a mental note to be sure to tell Toby, since this seemed to run counterintuitive to everything her Rom-Coms had told her.)”</i><br>It’s the first time I remember reading a book where the first date didn’t go in the most spectacular way. So thank you, Morgan Matson, for that!<br><br>But they have a good talk with one another when Andie comes over because of Bertie. I was so glad the dog recovered. And also glad for the really nice conversations they had while watching over Bertie.<br><br><i>“As Clark went on, telling his story, I realized that I wasn’t trying to stop him, or control the conversation, or keep him from asking me something I didn’t want to answer. It was like talking to my friends—and I would just have to see where the conversation took me. And so, surprising myself, I leaned forward to listen.”</i><br><br>Matson really knows how to develop her romances because just them holding hands for the first time left my heart beating too damn fast.<br><i>“I took a breath to continue the story when Clark’s hand brushed against mine, and all the words left my head.<br>I wasn’t sure if it was an accident, so I kept my hand stretched down by my side, within easy reach, and what felt like a lifetime later, Clark’s hand brushed mine again, sending a spark through me that I felt all the way in my toes. He kept his hand touching mine, and then, moving a millimeter at a time, curved his fingers around so that they were resting against my palm, just brushing it, so lightly. Then he moved up, over the curve of my thumb, and ran his index finger over the inside of my wrist in a slow circle.”</i><br><br>Meanwhile, the whole deal Toby made with Palmer concerning her excessive use of emojis made me crack up.<br><i>“You need to dial it back,” Palmer said as she pulled out her phone. “Like this afternoon, you texted me ‘I’m so whale, dancing girl, dancing girl, blushing smiley, nervous-teeth smiley, star, star, pizza.’ ” She looked up from her phone. “What was that supposed to mean?”</i><br>Seriously so entertaining.<br><br>Also also, a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18189606-since-you-ve-been-gone" rel="nofollow noopener">Since You’ve Been Gone</a> reference showed up:<br><i>“Whoa,” Palmer said, drawing back slightly from me, her expression surprised. “I mean,” she said, regrouping, “hi, Andie. Um . . . rough night?”<br>“Is it that bad?” I asked, tucking my hair behind my ears, slinking down farther in the booth. As I did, I caught the eye of a guy sitting across the restaurant and felt my stomach sink as he gave me a smile and a quick wave. It was Frank Porter, who I’d had a micro-crush on last year when I heard he broke up with his longtime girlfriend. But he came back to school in the fall so clearly besotted with Emily Hughes that I’d quashed my crush immediately. That still didn’t mean I wanted to look awful in front of him, though. He was sitting across from Matt Collins, who was saying something that made Frank laugh, and I turned my back on them.”</i><br>I’m so, so happy and I <b>really</b>want to reread it now.<br><br><i>“We’re doing a scavenger hunt, and we need something that has a business slogan with a pun,” I explained.<br>“Ah,” Dawn said, turning to Emily. “So you’re trying to check items off a list?” she asked, nudging her. “What’s that like?”<br>“Ignore my friend,” Emily said to us, rolling her eyes. “She’s inhaled too many pizza fumes today.”</i><br> I've missed them so much, why didn't I reread it before picking this up???<br><br>And the references to Matson's other books didn’t stop there, I was extremely giddy when all her characters randomly (and not so randomly) showed up. There were so many references and it made my heart lighter and my cheeks hurt from smiling too much. Thank you, thank you ,thank you. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462532946ra/19009118.gif" width="500" height="272" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And then when Andie finished Clark’s second book, I was cry-laughing over the texts she sent to her dad: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462532946i/19009119.png" width="520" height="480" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then it gets even better:<br><i>“Palmer and Tom both looked at Clark. “What did you do?” she asked.<br>“He killed Tamsin,” I said, glowering at him, while across the table from me, Palmer’s jaw dropped.<br>“You what?” she gasped.<br>“Fictionally,” Clark explained hurriedly. “It’s not like she was a real person.”<br>“Clearly not, to you,” I huffed.<br>“You bastard,” Tom said, now glaring at Clark as well.<br>“Wait, why are you upset?” Clark asked, sounding baffled.<br>“Because it’s all coming back to me now,” he said, shaking his head at Clark. “Really, how could you have done that?”</i><br>I absolutely love them. <br>The texts in this book were spectacular. Morgan has something special in each of her books, and this one did not miss out!<br><br>And speaking of Andie’s friends, I was amazed with how well all their friendships were written. Their group dynamics were pretty much all I could think about. It was both complex and lighthearted at times, especially with Bri and Toby—it was so great reading about such a close friendship. And even when they took a break, I was really glad for it. I could really relate to them and am extremely grateful that Morgan Matson ended it in that way.<br><br><i>“Do you know how horrible I’ve felt over the last two weeks?” Toby asked, turning to look at all of us. “It’s been the worst time of my life. And I couldn’t even talk to my best friend about it, since it was her fault.”<br>“I felt the same way—” Bri started, but Toby talked over her.<br>“I realized I don’t know who I am if I’m not your friend,” she said. “Like I have no idea at all. And that’s a problem.”<br>“So that’s it?” Bri asked, and I could hear the fear beneath her words. “We’re done?”<br>“Yes,” Toby said, her voice cracking. “I can’t do this anymore. I’m done.”</i><br>I was definitely crushed, but this was something so real that I couldn’t help but agree.<br><br><i>“I didn’t know what my life looked like if we weren’t all still friends. It was a reality I couldn’t even fully grasp. For the last five years, it had been the four of us, what I had always believed to be an unshakable unit. The thought of not having them—the thought of some reality I might have to accept where I didn’t have them—was making me feel like I wanted to scream, cry, and throw up, all at the same time.”</i><br>Those parts really hit home for me.<br><br><i>“And it was Maya’s words, coupled with severe boredom and loneliness, that led me to reach for my phone and scroll through my contacts until I got to Topher.<br>ME:<br>Hey. You around?<br>TOPHER:<br>It’s about time.”</i><br>So I have to mention it because it’s gonna really bother me if I don’t, but I absolutely hated Topher. I almost forgot that I did because we hadn’t focused on him for a while but the hate came back so quickly. Especially when he contacted her while she was with Clark. Topher just gave off a bad feeling.<br><br><i>"I could feel it happening, this pattern we always fell back into, but for some reason it didn’t feel like it normally did. It was feeling more like the time Bri accidentally took my shoes after a sleepover and I had to wear hers all day, aware with every step of how they didn’t fit me right.”</i><br>This description is so specific, yet weirdly relatable and accurate. How does Morgan do it??<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462534549ra/19009488.gif" width="500" height="218" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She clearly has a talent for writing incredible friendships:<br><i>“You know you can always come by.” Palmer nodded and took a breath. But before she could speak, I jumped in. “I really, really messed up,” I said. “I’m so sorry.”<br>“I know it was coming from a good place,” Palmer said, shaking her head. “But—”<br>“I know,” I said. “I was trying to control everything, because the thought of not having you guys . . .” I let out a shaky breath. “But I shouldn’t have interfered like that.”<br>Palmer nodded. “I know you were trying to help, in your own, very not helpful way,” she said, and I smiled. “But I overreacted. And I’m sorry, Andie.”</i><br>I really liked that we got some closure with those two. And there was a short roadtrip towards the end, which I’m all for. (I really want to reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7664334-amy-roger-s-epic-detour" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy &amp; Roger’s Epic Detour</a>.)<br><br>I just love how Morgan Matson weaves both friends and family in her books.<br>The situation with her dad started out rocky, but thanks to a supply of great movies and the warm weather, they started to bond— which, of course, melted my heart. I adore close families in books.<br><br>And I'm pretty happy with that ending, even if it was a bit cheesy. I can't wait to read more of Matson's future books, and hopefully reread her old ones.<br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Unexpected Everything</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1481404547/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=1481404547&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=ee363eb330083bc8524b9fd50f14511f" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928873i/21562486.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928873i/21562487.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Support creators you love. <div id="review_1630334408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630334408" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630334408?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630334408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18096631296949470635"><blockquote>
  <i>Clearly the downside of having a theoretical crush on someone you knew nothing about was the crashing realisation that you actually knew nothing about them.</i>
</blockquote><br/>This is my third and favourite read by Matson, despite the 3-star rating. In the past, I have found myself liking Matson's premises and her writing style, but being put off by the immaturity of her characters. In my opinion, they are 17/18 year olds with the "voices" of 12 year olds. Fortunately, that wasn't a problem here.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17838528.The_Unexpected_Everything' title='The Unexpected Everything by Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Unexpected </a></span>
  <span id="freeText18096631296949470635" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Clearly the downside of having a theoretical crush on someone you knew nothing about was the crashing realisation that you actually knew nothing about them.</i>
</blockquote><br />This is my third and favourite read by Matson, despite the 3-star rating. In the past, I have found myself liking Matson's premises and her writing style, but being put off by the immaturity of her characters. In my opinion, they are 17/18 year olds with the "voices" of 12 year olds. Fortunately, that wasn't a problem here.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17838528.The_Unexpected_Everything" title="The Unexpected Everything by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unexpected Everything</a> is, for the most part, a really good book. It manages to straddle the line between <b>fun summer beach read</b> and a <b>deeper contemporary about family life</b>. It appears to be something of a romance - and it sure is, to a certain extent - but it's also at least as much about friendship, growing up, loss and family.<br /><br />The narrator is Andie - a congressman's daughter whose life starts to unravel in the wake of her father's political scandal. She's Type A, ambitious and independent, and up until this point, she had everything figured out months in advance. Now her carefully-constructed world is crumbling and she finds herself forced to fill the summer gap in her resume by walking dogs.<br /><br /><b>I actually found the sympathy Matson constructs around Andie to be realistic and genuine</b>. It didn't even matter to me that, on a surface level, Andie was a white, privileged narrator. I felt for her when she discovered that even after working so hard, walking the line and doing everything right, factors beyond her control could just come flying in and ruin it all.<br /><br />The way her father's career has affected her life is told so well, as is their relationship. I loved the family parts of the book most of all, and enjoyed how the author turned Andie's father into a frustrating, obtuse, but oddly likable human being who is dealing with his own pain. This book could have turned into a stream of Andie angst, but it's cleverer and more thought-provoking than that.<br /><br />There are also many great friendships in the novel, further solidifying this as a book more about the process of being a teenager and growing up, than it is about that cute boy over there. The cute boy surfaces, of course, but he is dorky and awkward, which made a nice change from all the smirking bad boys who've had hundreds of girls before they've even made it out of high school.<br /><br />It's <b>a sensitive and fun novel</b>; not nearly as melodramatic as it easily could have been, but still important too. <br /><br />Okay, so the big question: <b>why only 3 stars?</b> Well, all of the positives I've listed above were notes I made during the first half of this book. <br /><br />The sad truth is, <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17838528.The_Unexpected_Everything" title="The Unexpected Everything by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unexpected Everything</a> is way too long</b>. I'm not exaggerating by saying that the book could have been cut in half. It's rare to find a contemporary YA that needs to be over 500 pages, and this one certainly didn't. I felt like we should have been approaching the finish line at the halfway point and so much of that second half <b>dragged</b>.<br /><br />I was enjoying the story so much and it was sad to see it dampened by slow, overlong stretches. Austen once said: <i>"if a book is well written, I always find it too short."</i> But I disagree. One of the things about writing a good book, series, or TV show, is knowing when to stop. Matson didn't get that here.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18096631296949470635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1415881753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415881753" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1415881753?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=summer-reads">summer-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1415881753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3978612802949612950"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17838528.The_Unexpected_Everything' title='The Unexpected Everything by Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Unexpected Everything</a> is the perfect summer read. I forgot we were still in April for a couple of hours. <br/><br/>Seventeen-year-old Andie, daughter of a congressman, is a <strong>dog walker</strong>.<br/><br/>Well, she didn’t plan on spending her summer running after dogs and making sure these fluffy buddies get their everyday amount of sun and exercise. Hell, she had a secure spot for a pre-med internship… before her letter of recommendation was withdrawn. Now she doesn’t know what to do—and since the best places are already</span>
  <span id="freeText3978612802949612950" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17838528.The_Unexpected_Everything" title="The Unexpected Everything by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unexpected Everything</a> is the perfect summer read. I forgot we were still in April for a couple of hours. <br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Andie, daughter of a congressman, is a <strong>dog walker</strong>.<br /><br />Well, she didn’t plan on spending her summer running after dogs and making sure these fluffy buddies get their everyday amount of sun and exercise. Hell, she had a secure spot for a pre-med internship… before her letter of recommendation was withdrawn. Now she doesn’t know what to do—and since the best places are already taken, all that was left for her was a position as a dog walker. The joy.<br /><br />She didn’t expect much from that job, especially not to meet a cute geek-looking guy who goes by the name of Clark. Like superman. But the thing is… Andie doesn’t date seriously. She’s all about having fun and isn’t ready let a guy infiltrate her heart and personal life. They’re awkward together. They don’t know how to behave in each other’s company. <strong>It’s adorable.</strong><br /><br />I only read one book by this author – though a ‘did not finish’ doesn’t quite count, does it? – and that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18189606.Since_You_ve_Been_Gone" title="Since You've Been Gone by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Since You've Been Gone</a>. I quickly realized that I was the black sheep, not being able to enjoy it like everyone else. Except, I’m the type of human being who believes in second chances, so I let myself be hyped up about this new contemporary novel.<br /><br />You know a story is enthralling, therefore worth finishing, when you can’t help yourself from peeking at it even during the most inappropriate moments. When someone’s talking to you, it’s clearly impolite to turn on your tablet and read a few sentences of Andie’s life, isn’t it? Well, my mind didn’t register that during those moments. I wanted to be as connected as possible to the story—book. Summer reads are usually the ones that put us in a high-spirited and sentimental mood; the sun, the beach, the romance, the warm weather, the joyful atmosphere and blather all provoke those sentiments.<br /><br />I find that, nowadays, contemporary young adult novels rarely reach five hundred pages, let alone exceed that amount. To be honest, it’s rare for me to not start losing interest in those monster books after the first hundred pages. To keep me interested, the said books have to contain 1 - <em>real </em>unforced humor, 2 – a relatable or entertaining heroine, 3 – three-dimensional secondary characters and 4 – a diverse series of events.<br /><br />This book is slow and five hundred thirty pages long, I’m not going to lie and pretend otherwise. It is what it is: a detailed account of Andie’s unexpected summer. <strong>Some parts are humorous, others more serious, most of them lent but the majority captivating.</strong> Andie and Clark make one hell of a diverting team. Do not fear, romance is not the only thing you will get out of it. It is also a story of family reunion. She and her politically invested dad are not the closest of pairs.<br /><br />For five years, he distanced himself from Andie and Andie never could mend the hole created in her heart. But now that he decided to take a break from anything politics-related, he’s determined to make amends for his lack of presence around his daughter. Those scenes are sweet. A father acting shyly around his own daughter may seem incongruous, but it’s reality for many people in this world. Personally, I found their renewed connection extremely sweet and was glad for the added theme of family by the author. It’s a favorite theme of mine.<br /><br /><strong>… But the book doesn’t deserve five stars. </strong>The main reason why it doesn’t is because of its unrealistic quality. Contemporaries <em>can</em> simply exist for our entertainment, period, but I could feel the author wanting to make this book as realistic as possible. It didn’t work. Not exactly. We do feel pulled in by Andie and enjoy following her ‘summer adventures’ but at the end of the day, we know that this isn’t imaginable and that it could never be us in Andie’s place. I prefer my contemporaries as close to real life as possible, but if you don’t mind a series of unrealistic coincidences, you’ll probably love this even more than I did.<br /><br /><strong> Regardless, I’m so glad I gave Morgan Matson a second chance. </strong><br /><br /><i>An advance copy of this book was provided to me by the publisher via Edelweiss.</i><br /><br /><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3978612802949612950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2305874857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305874857" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305874857?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305874857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10591038393105703203">there was a brief time when i thought i was outgrowing morgan matsons books. YA can be a fun genre for an old fart like me, but sometimes a story can feel a little too teenager-y and i was worried MM was heading in that direction. and although this book has some moments like that, im relieved to say i still enjoy her storytelling!<br/><br/>true to morgan matson style, this book is everything you want from a contemporary - its lighthearted, fluffy, and very carefree. but what i really enjoy most about her </span>
  <span id="freeText10591038393105703203" style="display:none">there was a brief time when i thought i was outgrowing morgan matsons books. YA can be a fun genre for an old fart like me, but sometimes a story can feel a little too teenager-y and i was worried MM was heading in that direction. and although this book has some moments like that, im relieved to say i still enjoy her storytelling!<br /><br />true to morgan matson style, this book is everything you want from a contemporary - its lighthearted, fluffy, and very carefree. but what i really enjoy most about her stories, and this one in particular, is the personal growth her MCs go through. i love the relationship andie has with her best friends (even if i did find some of them annoying), i think the closeness she develops with her father is very touching, and dont even get me started on clark. clark is literally book boyfriend goals personified. <i>swoon.</i><br /><br />this book is quite long for a YA novel, especially for being as predictable as it is, but i know the diehard MM fans will appreciate that. this is a story full of life, love, and everything in between - perfect for any upcoming summer TBR!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10591038393105703203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1299073691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299073691" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299073691?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299073691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14840572478194256350">Because the law <i>requires</i> me to make some sort of pun about the title here...<b>I MUST SAY, GOOD SIR, THIS WAS AN UNEXPECTED DELIGHT.</b> Except not <i>everything</i> was delightful. But lucky for your precious face, I'm going to have a list of likes and dislikes. But I'm very pleased to say that the book was <b>very sweet and happy.</b> I mean, plus drama and angst in the last 100-pages, but do you know how often I read HAPPY books???? Like 3% of the time. It was refreshing.<br/><br/>(Although FYI it is winter in Australia; a</span>
  <span id="freeText14840572478194256350" style="display:none">Because the law <i>requires</i> me to make some sort of pun about the title here...<b>I MUST SAY, GOOD SIR, THIS WAS AN UNEXPECTED DELIGHT.</b> Except not <i>everything</i> was delightful. But lucky for your precious face, I'm going to have a list of likes and dislikes. But I'm very pleased to say that the book was <b>very sweet and happy.</b> I mean, plus drama and angst in the last 100-pages, but do you know how often I read HAPPY books???? Like 3% of the time. It was refreshing.<br /><br />(Although FYI it is winter in Australia; and I realise the Americans are like "Oh let's publish nice summery books because it's summer!" but I am huddled under 74 blankets while forced to read your summer books and being murderously jealous. #AppreciateCaitsSuffering")<br /><br /><b> L I K E S:</b><br /><br /><b>• It is so so so so friendship focused!!</b><br />Seriously! Friendship is the BIGGEST THING in this book! (And I think that's really common for most of the Matson books I've read so far.) And ya know, this gives me warm fuzzies. Not only does it really hone in on Andie and her 3 really really close friends,<b> it talks about friendship between fathers and their daughters. </b>LIKE, AWWWWW. The book starts with Andie having like 2% of a relationship with her dad, and then it grows and strengthens until they're watching John Wayne (ew) and having midnight ice cream meetings and inside jokes and IT LITERALLY IS MY FAVOURITE THING TO WATCH THIS DAD AND HIS DAUGHTER GROW CLOSER.<br /><br /><b>• It features a HOMESCHOOLER who is NOT WEIRD.</b><br />Be still my beating heart. The love-interest is Clark who is a) a huge nerd, b) socially shy but not inept, c) a homeschool gradate, d) and a fantasy writer. AKA = HE IS THE MALE VERSION OF ME. He was so adorable and literally one of my FAVOURITE bookish boys of the universe!! He was funny and awkward and adorable and I shipped him and Andie so so so hard. Also Clark is suffering from writers block....which is like the ONLY way writers are represented in literature, so. That was annoying. But I appreciated all the insider writers jokes and how he felt with pressure from his fans and how he was so young and successful and ajdfklasdfjad CLARK. CLARK. CLARK. What I'm most impressed about is that he wasn't a FREAK. I could list a scanty few books/movies with homeschool characters, and usually the homeschooler is really embarrassingly freaky. WE ARE NOT, OKAY?!?! WE ARE COOL FISH SOMETIMES. DORKS AND NERDS, SURE, BUT NOT COMPLETE WEIRDOS.<br /><br /><b> • It was a relaly pleasant book to read.</b><br />I mean, <i>I</i> was stressing because when a book is about HAPPINESS I just am sitting there waiting for the sucker punch of tragedy. Ahem. But for about 400-pages, it was about a) strengthening summer friendships, b) Andie loosening her tight controlling reigns on relationships and letting herself fall for someone properly, and c) putting happiness first. I <i>loved</i> the theme of happiness. And it had that nice summery vibe with ice cream and scavenger hunts and pizza and pools...so, ya know, I'm here in winter being bitter BUT IT WAS ALSO NICE.<br /><br /><b> • DOGS! THERE ARE PUPPIES!!</b><br />Andie is set to go to pre-pre-med-med school (shhh, it's a thing) but gets dumped from the program at the last minute. She ends up walking dogs all summer. I KNOW. DREAM JOB. I am actually quitting being a writer directly and taking up dog walking because PUPPPPPIES. Ahem. So there are tons of dogs (and a few cats) here and none of them die, so isn't that lovely? So much win for the author here.<br /><br /><b>• I laughed out loud. SEVERAL TIMES.</b><br />The dialogue and witty banter was so freaking brilliant I CRACKED UP. Three or four times, and this is from the person who usually gives 1/3 of a smile and calls it laughing. NOPE. OUT LOUD. CRACKING. UP.<br /><br /><br /><b> D I S L I K E S:</b><br /><br />• <b>It was way too far freaking long.</b><br />I'm not gonna lie: I almost gave it 3 stars for this...why? Because <b>I got bored several times.</b> I realise it was building friendships and making the characters more complex with all the side detours but THERE WERE SO MANY RABBIT RUNS. Literally pages and pages of events that really didn't contribute to the plot. <b>Well...what plot, really?</b> It was a summery contemporary and full of laughs and sweet moments and romance, but definitely not excelling on the plot. But I found the first 100-pages excruciatingly boring, and then the middle just made me want to nap. <b>Contemporaries DO NOT need to be 500-pages.</b> They just don't. No.<br /><br /><b>• It was entirely predictable.</b><br />I mean, look at it. You KNOW Andie is the "I dump him before he dumps me, and it only lasts 3 weeks max." sorta gal. So aka the book is going to be about the guy who steals her heart, right? And she has awesome friends....okay so something is going to happen there. She misses her mum. Great, she'll confront those emotions. MAYBE I'vE JSUT READ TOO MUCH. But I think a lot of the reason I got bored was because it was entirely predictable.<br /><br /><b>• I was kind of disbelieving at how quickly it went from SUMMER! FUN! POPSICLES! to ANGST! DRAMA! HEARTBREAK!</b><br />Okay, I shouldn't be. Humans are weird and confusing, obviously. But the ending had me blinking quite rapidly and going "Seriously? After this whole summer of fun, you're gonna do THAT?" I just did NOT feel the ending at. all. I think this is because the climactic drama revolved around a secondary character, not Andie. So it felt detached from her and I didn't really <i>care</i>. (I mean, it does affect Andie and she ends up doing STUPID THINGS BECAUSE OF IT...but it felt like this whirlwind of STUPID because I wasn't invested in the secondary character as much as Andie.<br /><br /><br /><b>...All in all? It was definitely a sweet, summery book about friendship!</b><br />I won't even deny that I enjoyed that a lot! (I miss me zombies and stabbings though.) But the predictability and the length did give me lots of YAWN moments. However, puppies and ice cream and the cutest fantasy writer love interest to ever grace literature MORE than make up for that. <br /><br /><br />*** QUOTES ****<br /><br /><blockquote>Books were <i>everywhere</i>. Not in haphazard piles -- there was absolutely nothing about this place that seemed haphazard - but there were floor-to-ceiling built-ins on all sides of this very large room, and they were absolutely crammed with books. It was the kind of room -- big couches, comfy chairs -- that you would expect a TV in, but I didn't see one anywhere. All I could see were books.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote> "What is this?" I asked, taking it from him, then recognising the familiar font on the cover. This one showed a crow and a flaming swords. <i>A Murder of Crows,</i> the title read. <i>By C.B. McCallister.</i><br />"I know you don't read," Clark said, and I raised an eyebrow at him. "But I thought maybe you wouldn't have anything against <i>listening</i>. It's the audiobooks, so it's like someone telling you a story."<br />"Ha ha," I said, turning it over and reading the back. I felt my eyes widen. "this takes nineteen <i>hours</i>?"<br />"Yeah," Clark said, not seeming fazed by this. "And those are just the first two discs. There's like twelve, but I didn't want to scare you."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I'd found my favourite brand of plastic bag --orange, biodegradable, from Raiders of the Lost Bark, whose name thrilled Bri to no end. She'd almost lost it when I'd told her about the other business, Temple of Groom.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote> I was listening to it constantly -- in my car, in my room, before I went to bed, my phone propped up on my nightstand and a sleep timer on so I wouldn't miss anything. But the place I really loved to have the story told to me was while I was at work. There was something wonderful about being outside, moving, keeping an eye on the dogs in front of me while the rest of me was swept up in the story. As a direct result of this, all my dogs were getting much longer walks than normal, since I hated to stop in the middle of a really great part. The walks that were normally twenty minutes had turned into epic walks that took us all over town, and as a result, most of them were getting pretty wiped out.<br />"Well, it sure looks like they had fun," Maya said as she bent down and scratched BAnjo's ears. Banjo immediately flipped onto his back and looked at her expectantly -- he was a fool for belly rubs.<br />"Definitely," I lied, since I honestly couldn't have told her. Tamsin had been captured by the book's great villain, locked in a tower, and separated from the Elder, so the amount of fun the dogs were having had not been my primary concern.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14840572478194256350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646923553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4820035578584501522"><br/><b>On sale for $1.99 on kindle 1/15/2017 Another one of my favs</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465319751i/19340510._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is so good and it made me cry. Okay, I know, I always say that, but I always cry in books whether it's happy or sad.<br/><br/>You have Andie who's father is a politician and they haven't really spent time together in about 5 years. Andie's mom isn't around but you can read about that in the book. I love Andie's friends. Palmer, Toby and Bri are all best friends with Andie and yes those are girls. :-) They have Tom and Wyatt as the guy f</span>
  <span id="freeText4820035578584501522" style="display:none"><br><b>On sale for $1.99 on kindle 1/15/2017 Another one of my favs</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465319751i/19340510._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is so good and it made me cry. Okay, I know, I always say that, but I always cry in books whether it's happy or sad.<br><br>You have Andie who's father is a politician and they haven't really spent time together in about 5 years. Andie's mom isn't around but you can read about that in the book. I love Andie's friends. Palmer, Toby and Bri are all best friends with Andie and yes those are girls. :-) They have Tom and Wyatt as the guy friends. <br><br>Andie has it all planned out for the summer. She's going to the Young Scholars Program at John Hopkins, but there is a big scandal with her father and she gets turned down. I mean seriously, this had nothing to do with Andie and it isn't fair but that's life. And her father wasn't guilty either but it is what it is right? <br><br>Now Andie has no idea what she's going to do, but her friends are happy she's going to be with them over the summer. Andie decides to at least apply for a job and this happens to be in the form of a dog walker :-) Yes, doggers! I love it! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465320889i/19340652._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of the dogs she walks is Bertie the Great Pyrenees. She actually meets Bertie and his caretaker, Clark Bruce McCallister, when Bertie got away from him and sort of had a run in with Andie. She wasn't a dog walker at the time, but when Clark found out she had a job walking dogs she hired the company she was working through. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465320889i/19340653.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At first Andie is really down that she had to stay home for the summer, but it turns out to be the best summer EVER! Her dad is home now and they got off to a bad start but then it ended up really great for them. I was so happy for them in the book. Andie has a great time with her friends. AND.... there is always the AND... she finds love with wonderful Clark. I love Clark. He's a teenage fantasy writer (yeah teenage writer!) and he's dreamy. <br><br>Watching Andie and Clark slowly get together was so sweet. <br><br><b>---&gt;EXCERPT&lt;---<br><br>I wasn't sure if it was an accident, so I kept my hand stretched down by my side, within easy reach, and what felt like a lifetime later, Clark's hand brushed mine again, sending a spark through me that I felt all the way in my toes. He kept his hand touching mine, and then, moving a millimeter at a time, curved his fingers around so that they were resting against my palm, just brushing it, so lightly. Then he moved up, over the curve of my thumb, and ran his index finger over the inside of my wrist in a slow circle. I could feel my pulse fluttering beneath his fingertips, and I had to remind myself that I knew how to breathe, that I'd been doing it my whole life. And then our palms were touching, perfectly lined up, though I could feel how much bigger his hand was than mine, feel his fingertips curving over the tops of mine, despite what Bri had always called my "weird large tree-frog hands." We stayed that way for just a moment, and then, like we'd talked about it before, like we'd mutually picked the time, our fingers interlocked and we were holding hands.</b><br><br>OMG, I could be in that moment and then they walked and talked. They at one point FINALLY kissed and it was "ahhhhhhhhhh." Yeah, I'm a little/alot crazy! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465320889i/19340654.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though there were so many fun things that happen in the book, there are the upsetting things. The things brought up about unhappy pasts, things that happen within the group of friends, but we always have to take the bad with the good. Even in a book or if it's too bad you can just throw the book across the room or something. <br><br>Either way, I loved the book, the characters, the whole story line. I hope Morgan Matson keeps popping these books out. I want more and more! ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/06/the-unexpected-everything-by-morgan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

I really enjoyed so many aspects of this book overall, but there were just some annoying things I couldn't ignore. <br/><br/>From the beginning,<b> I couldn't bring myself to like or relate to Andie.</b> Politician's privileged </span>
  <span id="freeText7898015396008849495" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<b>"I looked up at him, and a thought passed through my brain before I could stop or analyze it.</b><i> It’s you—of course it is. There you are."</i><br><br>♥ buddy read with my favorite, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/23218431-sharon" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharon</a> ♥<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468452933ra/19708555.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br><b>3.5 stars.</b> Because of all the hype surrounding Morgan Matson &amp; her books, <i>my high expectations just weren't met</i>. I really enjoyed so many aspects of this book overall, but there were just some annoying things I couldn't ignore. <br><br>From the beginning,<b> I couldn't bring myself to like or relate to Andie.</b> Politician's privileged daughter who at one point almost doesn't take a dog-walking job because she feels like she's above it.....<i> How was I supposed to ignore that? </i><b>THANKFULLY</b>, Andie does show some character development, and I loved the way her relationships with her friends, Clark, and father evolved. <br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468810932ra/19747783.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br><b>Enter Clark.</b> Aka nerdy, sweet, kinda awkward fantasy writer. *cough* dream guy *cough*. No, but really, <b>CLARK'S EVERYTHING</b>. He was always so honest about his thoughts and feelings &amp; I found him to be the best part of this book because of that. There was no drama in his department, unless it was Andie who was starting it lmao.<br><br><b>Some other great parts of the story were:</b><br><br><b>ANDIE'S FRIEND GROUP. </b>Omg. So, so cute. Palmer, Toby, and Bri were such different individuals, but they understood each other so well &amp; were so supportive of each other through everything. I loved their little rituals, their little texting convos, etc. So cute.<br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468811068ra/19747804.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br><b>Andie + her father</b>. I cannot stress how much I disliked her father in the beginning. He's the typical 'fake' dad who acts like he's there to everyone, but really isn't. And then suddenly he tries to be strict w/ Andie after realizing she's practically been raising herself.... OK THEN. Their growth was everything though. It was one of my favorite parts of the story, so no spoiling from me!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b> ❝“And Clark stole my keys, so I might need to borrow your car.”<br>“He did?” my dad asked, starting to smile.<br>I frowned at him, and his expression grew more serious. <br>“I mean, of course he shouldn’t have done that to you. ❞</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Overall, a good book imo! I expected more romance, but despite that I don't think <i>the lack of it</i> was what made this a 3-star read. <b>It was mainly Andie being annoying lmao.</b> I wouldn't tell anyone to clear their tbr lists for this one, <u>but I liked it</u>. I will definitely try to read more of Matson's stuff in the future, though :D</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627430915" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1627430915?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627430915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7371078910775078378">I just...didn’t care about this book.<br/><br/>And I feel like I really should have?? It’s a Morgan Matson book, for one thing. Also, the main character is a dog walker. Also also, the love interest is a nerdy writer (!!!) and there’s a solid group of friends at the core and there’s a lot of texting. And if anyone knows anything about me, it should be that I inexplicably love when texting is incorporated into books. These are all very good things.<br/><br/>BUT NONE OF IT CLICKED.<br/><br/>All of it felt so eh. Andie, the mai</span>
  <span id="freeText7371078910775078378" style="display:none">I just...didn’t care about this book.<br /><br />And I feel like I really should have?? It’s a Morgan Matson book, for one thing. Also, the main character is a dog walker. Also also, the love interest is a nerdy writer (!!!) and there’s a solid group of friends at the core and there’s a lot of texting. And if anyone knows anything about me, it should be that I inexplicably love when texting is incorporated into books. These are all very good things.<br /><br />BUT NONE OF IT CLICKED.<br /><br />All of it felt so eh. Andie, the main character, full-on does not do it for me. I think she was probably intended to be a character kind of unlike those we get in YA, but instead she just felt like the any-person flat undeveloped contemporary girls of any 2013 romance, who are just a blank slate for preteens everywhere to project themselves onto while the boy gets some devilish edgy archetype.<br /><br />Minus the devilish boy part.<br /><br />I did like the circle of friends, and I truly wish we got even more time with them. Which isn’t to say we didn’t get a lot, because we did. Mainly I’d just read about the internal workings of the relationship dynamic between the waitresses at the diner they frequent if that meant getting out of Andie’s head more often.<br /><br />And while I really wanted to like Clark, the aforementioned nerdy-writer-subject-of-romancin’, I didn’t. He also felt kind of underdeveloped and boring. As did Andie’s father, and her relationship with him, even though that takes up a lot of the book.<br /><br />Basically, I think I am astonished at the fact that this book could casually be exactly eight thousand seven hundred and forty-two pages long (or 519, same difference) and still feel so flat/boring/underdone/half-baked/overwhelmingly <i>eh</i>.<br /><br />Having said that, this book was still written by Morgan Matson, which means it feels like summer and takes thirty seconds to read and will always have at least occasional seconds of fun and one to two heart-wrenching Emotional Speeches And/Or Moments.<br /><br />Which puts it above most contemporaries anyway.<br /><br />Bottom line: Not my favorite Morgan Matson!!! But still by Morgan Matson.<br /><br />-----------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />the reread-every-morgan-matson-book-before-her-new-one-comes-out-a-thon is: COMPLETE.<br /><br />the emotional turmoil that was that bonanza comes to an unbearably meh finish with this book.<br /><br />or in other words: oh my god this book was so <i>eh.</i><br /><br />review to come</span>

    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944051973?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-bought-in-2016">books-bought-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=summertime">summertime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-multiple-book-series-by-author">read-multiple-book-series-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=released-in-2016">released-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-girl">pov-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=stand-alones">stand-alones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944051973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15060121735600156659">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a> <br/><br/><u>
  <b>AFTER READING</b>
</u><br/><b>MY THOUGHTS</b><br/>I was looking for a feel-good read and thought that Morgan Matson would be a great choice and this is one that I hadn't yet reread. It also has puppers, a character who writes, and it takes place in the summer, so it really felt like a perfect book to reread! Rereading this book I realized that there were so many details I still retained but I still immensely enjoyed reading it! Some things were different than </span>
  <span id="freeText15060121735600156659" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a> <br /><br /><u>
  <b>AFTER READING</b>
</u><br /><b>MY THOUGHTS</b><br />I was looking for a feel-good read and thought that Morgan Matson would be a great choice and this is one that I hadn't yet reread. It also has puppers, a character who writes, and it takes place in the summer, so it really felt like a perfect book to reread! Rereading this book I realized that there were so many details I still retained but I still immensely enjoyed reading it! Some things were different than I remember, but it's still a great Morgan Matson book. <br /><br />Andie's plans include an all-important internship at a med school. Not only will it help her future and look good on a resume, but it lets her out of the house after her dad (a congressman) got involved with a scandal. But when said scandal causes Andie to get pulled from an internship, she doesn't know what to do. All of the other internships and jobs are already taken and she can't have a gap in her resume. She has to find something to do and sure it wasn't walking dogs, but maybe she can find greatness in this summer after all. <br /><br />This indeed has a lot of feel-good to it (the puppers help). One of the reasons why I love Morgan Matson's books is that while her books can sometimes be predictable, her books are incredibly realistic because there is complexity to them. Yes, this book has a romance in it, but it's not just about romance. There is a lot about trying to figure out what you are doing when the unexpected happens (which is definitely relatable) and trying new things. There are themes are sticking with your friends and fixing relationships. There is even Andie still dealing with her mother's death years later and the father that is so caught up in work that he has no time for her. Speaking of Andie, there was just so much growth in her character in the book and even growth in the characters surrounding her as the book progressed. <br /><br />The characters in this book are just fantastic! I loved seeing the group texts between Andie's friends! I also loved that Andie's dad was a part of the book and we see their relationship change from a nonexistent relationship to a close relationship. I honestly just loved seeing everyone react around each other. Again, it goes back to the complexity that Morgan Matson includes in her books. Each character is dynamic with their own unique personalities. They all feel like real people which made all of the emotions feel real. Let's not forget the dogs! I love love love dogs. If you asked me what my favorite animal was it would be, no question, dogs! So that was a big part of why I wanted to reread this book. Even the dogs get their personalities showcased! The main dog we see is Bertie who is a Great Pyrenees and I am just full of happiness just thinking about him! I volunteered walking dogs in the past and I kept getting reminded two Great Pyrenees, a brother and sister that the shelter was trying to get adopted together. They were just sweet furballs and I adored them. Thankfully they are now in a happy home!<br /><br />Okay, I'll stop talking about dogs (even though I don't want to) and get to what disappointed me during my reread. My first time reading I gave this 5 stars, this time it gets 4 stars. This is mainly is due to the last part of the book, which I completely forgot about. Near the end, there is a large portion where the feel-good drops and we get a lot of conflict. I don't have a problem with the fact that there is conflict, because in real life there is conflict, I have a problem with the reasons why there was a conflict. A lot of it seemed stupid, avoidable, and it took up a lot of space in the book (this isn't a short book) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[My main gripe is that there is conflict over the fact that one friend has a crush on a boy and it turns out that boy has a crush on another friend (and they strike up a relationship). Andie finds out about it and there is DRAMA. It was just so stupid. I'm not on either side, but WHY WOULD YOU LET A GUY RUIN A FRIENDSHIP! Because this actually ends a lifelong friendship, over a guy who was not worth it! WHY DO PEOPLE DO THIS?! Ugh. Frankly, it was also a bit cliche. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It really just made me frustrated.<br /><br /><b>IN CONCLUSION</b><br />Overall, I did enjoy rereading this book! Part of the later part frustrated me, but I just loved all the characters and the friendships and the puppers! This is a really great summertime read and I'm glad that I gave it another read!<br /><br /><u>
  <b>BEFORE READING</b>
</u><br />I don't even need to know what this book is about.<br /><b>IT IS BY MORGAN MATSON</b><br />It could be about purple unicorns and their adventures in a dentist office and I would still want to read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15060121735600156659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1594384471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1594384471" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544410363p2/14772037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1594384471?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone between the ages of 12 and 25</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=contemporary-reads">contemporary-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=fall-2016-tbr">fall-2016-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=best-2016-reads">best-2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1594384471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8181271881131721432"><b>5/5 STARS </b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469116341ra/19782617.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>What it is about!</b><br/>This book is a typical Morgan Matson book..meaning it is a wickedly realistic and an awesome contemporary. <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446680159ra/16865373.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This story surrounds the title character Andie (short for Alexandra) as her summer takes a surprising turn. With her summer plans ruined, Andie rushes to find something to do with her summer. Through scandals, love, family and friends this book definitely takes you on a wonderful journey. This story ventures into father-daughter relationships that are REAL, fun an</span>
  <span id="freeText8181271881131721432" style="display:none"><b>5/5 STARS </b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469116341ra/19782617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>What it is about!</b><br>This book is a typical Morgan Matson book..meaning it is a wickedly realistic and an awesome contemporary. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446680159ra/16865373.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This story surrounds the title character Andie (short for Alexandra) as her summer takes a surprising turn. With her summer plans ruined, Andie rushes to find something to do with her summer. Through scandals, love, family and friends this book definitely takes you on a wonderful journey. This story ventures into father-daughter relationships that are REAL, fun and relatable friendships and a true coming of age story. Andie learns a lot about herself and how to approach the world in this contemporary novel. She is experiences a lot of growth in many aspects of her life.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429279827ra/14563518.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b> My Review! Contains spoilers! </b><br>This book took me on a journey. I connected to the characters extremely well and found some of their situations realistic and how each of the characters reacted to situations to be extremely fascinating and understandable. The character development and little details make this book so refreshing. The little quirks of the MC, her friends, her dad and everyone else in her life really make the book worth while as they are seen in day to day life. I loved the writing, the story, the characters and especially the ending. It wasn't a happily ever after for all of the characters and it showed that things will change and some friendships won't last forever. I LOVED IT.<br><br>CLARK IS ONE OF THE BEST LOVE INTERESTS I HAVE EVER READ ABOUT IN A NOVEL! He is a huge dork, but decently built, writes fantasy novels, loves big romantic gestures and is a bit socially awkward. Toby has some super relatable lines even though she can be a bit annoying, but her friends accept her for it. Andie's relationship with her dad is weak and fragile at the beginning of the story and takes a really long time to repair. Do you know what's great about that? IT'S RELATABLE AND REAL! Her life isn't perfect, her relationships with the people around her or how she conducts herself isn't perfect. She has her insecurities, her trust issues, her comfort zone. She has her likes, dislikes and where she draws the line. <br><br>This novel will draw you right into the characters. It's a smooth read and extremely enjoyable. I recommend you guys pick it up and try it! Then tell me what you thought!!!</span>
