              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806331201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7041009306897714770"><br/><b> Maybe 4.5 stars! ;) </b><br/><br/>As expected from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson' title='Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Morgan Matson</a>, it is <b>
  <i>“Everything Unexpected”</i>
</b> and perhaps my most delightful read from the author as to date. It’s the perfect encompassing summer story about family, friendship, relationships, moving on from loss of a loved one, falling in love, making important life decisions and embarking on new adventures. It’s a lot more fun than I expected it to be. Although the story sometimes read a bit like rom-com movies making it a bit predictable, it was still</span>
  <span id="freeText7041009306897714770" style="display:none"><br /><b> Maybe 4.5 stars! ;) </b><br /><br />As expected from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson" title="Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Morgan Matson</a>, it is <b>
  <i>“Everything Unexpected”</i>
</b> and perhaps my most delightful read from the author as to date. It’s the perfect encompassing summer story about family, friendship, relationships, moving on from loss of a loved one, falling in love, making important life decisions and embarking on new adventures. It’s a lot more fun than I expected it to be. Although the story sometimes read a bit like rom-com movies making it a bit predictable, it was still very enjoyable and heartwarming. (I can’t stop laughing at Toby’s emoji language). <br /><br />I especially appreciate the themes on taking life one day at a time and accepting risks and challenges because these things are really what life is all about. I also love that the story is very realistic and yet it still manages to have fantastical elements to it. You’ll get what I mean when you read the book. And most of all, I love that there are dogs in it, on the cover no less! (It’s one of the reasons I bought the book. ;). I just love Morgan Matson- her kind and wonderful personality that her writing and stories naturally exude. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7041009306897714770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1742051516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1742051516" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742051516?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146145" href="/book/show/29415084-the-unexpected-everything">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who's looking for a light and cute read!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasmine by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=practical-methods">practical-methods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=happy-ending">happy-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=preciously-owned">preciously-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=realism">realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742051516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15790201536919297396"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Sometimes we get a little bit of a facade. We think we have people. Family, friends...but in the end, it's just you and the darkness. Everyone leaves eventually, my young friend. It's better, really, to learn it early. This way, you can save yourself some disappointment."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>The Unexpected Everything</i> is my first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson' title='Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Morgan Matson</a> book. Technically, it's supposed to be the second, because I once tried to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7664334.Amy___Roger_s_Epic_Detour' title='Amy & Roger's Epic Detour by Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amy & Roger's Epic Detour</a> but didn't like it then. However, after finishing this on</span>
  <span id="freeText15790201536919297396" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Sometimes we get a little bit of a facade. We think we have people. Family, friends...but in the end, it's just you and the darkness. Everyone leaves eventually, my young friend. It's better, really, to learn it early. This way, you can save yourself some disappointment."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>The Unexpected Everything</i> is my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson" title="Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Morgan Matson</a> book. Technically, it's supposed to be the second, because I once tried to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7664334.Amy___Roger_s_Epic_Detour" title="Amy &amp; Roger's Epic Detour by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy &amp; Roger's Epic Detour</a> but didn't like it then. However, after finishing this one, I definitely will give her other books a shot. <b>What I really, really love about this book is that I can relate to almost everything in it and let's say the story touches my heart deeply.</b> <br><br>Normally, YA Contemporary isn't a genre I'd go for when choosing a book but who knows? I think I'm just lucky enough to pick the right one and it soon becomes one of my all-time-favorites. <i>The Unexpected Everything</i> tells a story of a teenage girl, Andie, who <i>always</i> sticks to her plan and maps out her future beforehand. But when her summer program is cancelled at the last minute, she suddenly doesn't know what to do next. She's completely lost and well, that's how everything unexpected drops from the sky. <br><br>For example, she never thinks she'll end up <i>walking dogs</i>--real dogs--for an entire summer instead of preparing for her pre-med courses in some sort of prestigious school, nor will she consider getting a longer-than-three-week boyfriend in the process. I like that books bring them closer and makes their relationship stronger, because well, apparently when a guy who <i>writes/reads</i> meets a girl who <i>doesn't read</i>...they'll find a way out eventually. #bookwormproblems <blockquote>I nodded, like this was normal, to hear someone my age talking about their <i>readers</i>. "So what is it?"<br>"Oh," Clark said, and adjusted his glasses quickly. He tilted his head slightly to the side, like he was trying to figure something out. "You're not...I assume you haven't read them."<br><b>I shook my head. "I don't really read, you know, books." Clark's eyebrows flew up, and it was like he took a step back from me, even though I was pretty sure his feet didn't actually move.</b> "I know how to <i>read</i>," I said, seeing the alarm in his expression. "I just don't love fiction. You know, novels."<br>"If you don't love fiction novels," Clark said, and even though I tried to fight it, I could feel a smile tugging at the corners of my mouth, "what do you read?" <b>He shook his head, and it was like I could practically feel how baffled he was. "Wait, I'm sorry, but how do you not read books? Like--what do you do on planes?"</b>
</blockquote><br>Another thing I like about their relationship is that both of them are <b>super awkward</b> in lots of situations. The first time they talk, their first coincidence, their first date...etc. Unsurprisingly, it's not often seen in other stories because most of the time, fiction isn't reality. But in this book, the author describes every single detail occurring in our lives really well, as if telling us that it's fine to be awkward, and there's nothing perfect in the real world! <blockquote>"So," he said, and I held my breath, feeling my heart pound in my chest. "Do you think you might want to, I don't know...try the dinner thing again?"<br>I felt myself smile, big and dorky and taking over my face. "Yes," I said without hesitating. There didn't seem to be any point in pretending I had plans or telling him I'd have to get back to him.</blockquote><br>As for Andie's group of friends, in my opinion, it's probably what makes me love the story so much. <b>Sometimes we take our friendship for granted and forget how precious it is, how much it means to us, and not until something terrible threatens it do we realize the importance of its presence.</b> In the story, Andie has her beloved childhood friends, Toby, Bri, Palmer, Tom, and Wyatt, since years and years ago. She used to think they'll stay as besties forever, that nothing can destroy their bond...until a harsh truth is discovered and unfortunately, wrecks everything. Therefore, it seems like her life is crumbling all of a sudden and once again, she does not expect any of these to happen.<br><br>Fortunately, while her friendship may not be as solid and perfect as the old days, her relationship with her congressman dad improves day by day. I'm genuinely happy for her, because somehow I know the feeling of being ignored in a family. Take my aunt for example, she's a journalist and a total workaholic so when I was little, I seldom saw her in daytime, or even when I did, she'd be busy listening to CNN and reading lots of newspaper at the same time. She never speaks to me willingly, and always asks the same questions like "When does the school start?" or "Have you read the article about how to lead a successful life I just sent you?" Thus, I kind of get used to her indifference towards our family members and don't expect anything more than <s>warm</s> greetings whenever I see her.<br><br>To sum up, <i>The Unexpected Everything</i> is a book about family, friends, and love along with every trifle in daily life that warms and breaks your heart, makes you laugh and cry; above all, it'll encourage you to take the first step and help you grow up. So, I <b>highly recommend</b> it to everyone who's looking for a light, fun and simple read. :) Now if you'll excuse me, I'm going to strategize the best dog walking routine that'll somehow end up meeting a cute Dogboy soon! *wink wink*<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472722951i/20232125.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15790201536919297396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17369439632897118258">This was very sweet, I loved the message behind it, and come on, how often do we get a 500+ page YA contemporary romance?! The writing was wonderful, as expected and Morgan Matson fans will delight in this (plus it's total nerd girl reading porn - you'll get what I mean when you read it.) Personally though, the romance was just not for me and I never connected to it or the love interest - and since that's the main narrative I really couldn't give it more than 3 stars. I very much enjoyed the fam</span>
  <span id="freeText17369439632897118258" style="display:none">This was very sweet, I loved the message behind it, and come on, how often do we get a 500+ page YA contemporary romance?! The writing was wonderful, as expected and Morgan Matson fans will delight in this (plus it's total nerd girl reading porn - you'll get what I mean when you read it.) Personally though, the romance was just not for me and I never connected to it or the love interest - and since that's the main narrative I really couldn't give it more than 3 stars. I very much enjoyed the family and friend dynamic of this novel though, as I always do with Morgan Matson's work.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=all-time-favs">all-time-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=shipshipship">shipshipship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=great-female-characters">great-female-characters</a>,

<div id="review_1813161638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813161638" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813161638?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rachel Reads Ravenously by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813161638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16064729157956483438"><b> 4 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “You have to try. You have to take your chances. Go and attempt and see what happens. And even if you fail - especially if you fail - come back with your experience and your hard-won knowledge and a story you can tell. And then later you can say, without regret or hesitation... 'Once, I dared to dare greatly” </i> </b><br/><br/>Morgan Matson has proven once again she is the queen of contemporary young adult novels for girls. This book is the story of Andie, responsible daughter of a politician recentl</span>
  <span id="freeText16064729157956483438" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “You have to try. You have to take your chances. Go and attempt and see what happens. And even if you fail - especially if you fail - come back with your experience and your hard-won knowledge and a story you can tell. And then later you can say, without regret or hesitation... 'Once, I dared to dare greatly” </i> </b><br><br>Morgan Matson has proven once again she is the queen of contemporary young adult novels for girls. This book is the story of Andie, responsible daughter of a politician recently under fire from the press. When her scheduled summer plans fall through, she's left without a plan for what to do with her life for the summer. Every one of her friends already have plans, and Andie finds a job as a dog walker. What lies ahead is a summer of learning new things, romance and the test of friendship.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456556813i/18248686.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> <i> “I could do this. If whole galaxies could change, so could I.” </i> </b><br><br>I really enjoyed this book, I think like Matson's other books it gives teen readers a hint that life isn't all you plan it to be and to sometimes let things go and see what happens. The beginning was pretty slow, I really had to push to get to a point where the book really flowed. My favorite parts of the book were when Andie and her father spent time together and learning more about the character of Clark. I like that the author brought in a quirky, nerdy hero instead of some kind of life guard stud or something. Yay for the nerd boys!<br><br>I was very much enthralled by the book, but once I put it down I noticed some things didn't match up entirely. There were subplots that seemed to go nowhere, friendship drama that seemed unnecessary except for the sake of drama, and this book was way too long. I had a few moments where I wondered if long paragraphs were important to the plot (spoiler alert, they weren't). But this is a fantastic teen contemporary read, great for the summer time. Once I got in the flow of things I found it hard to put this book down!<br><br><b> <i> “The idea that you could rethink the thing you'd always thought you wanted and change your plan - it was almost a revolutionary concept. That you could choose what would make you happy, not successful." </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455783307i/18148833._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16064729157956483438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837131636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17719480066230921815">This was maybe my very favorite Morgan Matson book. It was the perfect blend of friendship, family relationships, and a really touching romance that I loved watching unfold. Andie is the daughter of a congressman, and never lets things get serious with any guy. <br/><br/>When her father gets investigated, and her summer internship falls through, they are stuck together for the summer, and she winds up meeting a cute guy, Clark, while dog walking. This one is ADORABLE if you are a pet lover. Bertie, the ma</span>
  <span id="freeText17719480066230921815" style="display:none">This was maybe my very favorite Morgan Matson book. It was the perfect blend of friendship, family relationships, and a really touching romance that I loved watching unfold. Andie is the daughter of a congressman, and never lets things get serious with any guy. <br /><br />When her father gets investigated, and her summer internship falls through, they are stuck together for the summer, and she winds up meeting a cute guy, Clark, while dog walking. This one is ADORABLE if you are a pet lover. Bertie, the main dog character, is such a cutie. And so is watching Andie work things out with her dad. One of the best summer-themed reads I’ve found! <br /><br />Please excuse typos/name misspellings. Entered on screen reader.</span>

<div id="review_1240887060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240887060" />
    <a title="Liam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34270521-liam"><img alt="Liam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415266097p2/34270521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240887060?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam" href="/user/show/34270521-liam">Liam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146145" href="/book/show/29415084-the-unexpected-everything">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34270521-liam?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240887060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17020330332286280629">It only took me 20 pages to know that I was going to love this book... And after 517 pages I can safely say it fully deserves a solid 5 star rating!<br/><br/>I wanted a cute, realistic, summer read and that's exactly what I got! Morgan Matson has done it yet again!<br/><br/>From start to finish this book honestly felt so real. The characters and their relationships were so well written and it was almost as though I'd known this gang of amazing characters for years! I related to all of the characters in different wa</span>
  <span id="freeText17020330332286280629" style="display:none">It only took me 20 pages to know that I was going to love this book... And after 517 pages I can safely say it fully deserves a solid 5 star rating!<br /><br />I wanted a cute, realistic, summer read and that's exactly what I got! Morgan Matson has done it yet again!<br /><br />From start to finish this book honestly felt so real. The characters and their relationships were so well written and it was almost as though I'd known this gang of amazing characters for years! I related to all of the characters in different ways and I honestly loved each one! Their group chats messages had me smiling from ear to ear and the use of emojis was just so on point! I loved how there was both boys and girls in the main group of friends, it was nice to see a mix of genders and personalities.<br /><br />I was loving this book already but then my love massively increased when the nerdy, super kind guy comes along! I honestly related to Clark so much and I could see myself being great friends with him and Tom. Clark and Andie are the cutest fictional couple I've met in a while, they're just so great for each other and I rooted for them from the start!<br /><br />Another thing I thought this book did brilliantly was the character's relationships with their parents! I feel like you never really get to know the parents in YA novels, they're either non existent or happy clappy, but in this book the relationships were real, honest and well developed!<br /><br />Although I did find myself rolling my eyes at how predictable some parts were I literally did not care because I felt as they added to the whole experience of the book! At first I was expected it to drag as it's pretty big for a YA book but honesty it's such an easy and enjoyable read you won't want it to end!<br /><br />It's safe to say that I will be reading any book Morgan Matson writes in the future! Her books never fail to make me realise how precious life is and how much we should value each other! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17020330332286280629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1615025239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1615025239" />
    <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd"><img alt="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479923328p2/11177071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615025239?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd">Kelly (Diva Booknerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146145" href="/book/show/29415084-the-unexpected-everything">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=simon-schuster">simon-schuster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=bookgasm">bookgasm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615025239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7513422425625686954">The Unexpected Everything was an incredible story of firsts and finding your own feet. Andie seemingly has it all, a wonderful group of friends, living in a beautiful home, intelligent, beautiful but unpretentious. But five years ago, Andie lost both of her parents. Her mother to ovarian cancer, while her father campaigned for the community, a congressman who left nannies and advisors to raise his grieving teen daughter. Now he's home pending the corruption investigation and for Andie, it's too </span>
  <span id="freeText7513422425625686954" style="display:none">The Unexpected Everything was an incredible story of firsts and finding your own feet. Andie seemingly has it all, a wonderful group of friends, living in a beautiful home, intelligent, beautiful but unpretentious. But five years ago, Andie lost both of her parents. Her mother to ovarian cancer, while her father campaigned for the community, a congressman who left nannies and advisors to raise his grieving teen daughter. Now he's home pending the corruption investigation and for Andie, it's too little too late. One of the loveliest aspects of The Unexpected Everything was the relationship between Andie and her father. Slowly and through perseverance, they begin to repair their tentative relationship and help one another through the grief they both share. It felt so lovingly written and realistic, leaving me reflecting on my own life and a father who refused to relate to his own daughters.<br /><br />Andie's circle of friends were hilarious. Each incredibly well developed with their own quirks and personalities. They are supportive on not only Andie, but also one another. So when Andie stumbles upon Clark, quite literally, there's no jealousy or backhanded compliments, just genuine support for their friend. It was so incredibly refreshing. Lately it seems that so many young adult novels enjoy creating toxic friendships between it's female characters, which I know during your teen years is realistic but also needs to be balanced by positive female friendships and The Unexpected Everything is a wonderful example.<br /><br />Clark although slightly older than Andie, was the epitome of a book boyfriend. He's not described as a vision of physical perfection, he's often painfully shy and although not having completed his education, is a young and acclaimed author who has landed in Andie's in the hope of braving his writers block. Oh how I loved Clark. He and his placid yet monstrous companion in Bertie seemed to be a calming influence in Andie's life, and for the first time Andie also believes in the possibility of falling in love.<br /><br />Morgan Matson has crafted an incredibly and light hearted contemporary that also touches on real issues, such as absent or working parents, the scrutiny that teens face and the friendships that bind one another. It was not only sex positive with Andie and Clark having discussed the physical aspects of their relationship, but menstruation. It's rare to find a young adult title that mentions it beyond a tampon spilling from a characters handbag, and even then it's painted as a horrifying experience. I adored the romance. Not only between Andie and Clark, but also Andie's best friend Palmer and her long term boyfriend Tom. I loved the group dynamics and friend Toby who was forced to spend the summer unable to text, but rather could only communicate through emoji images. I had no clue what she was saying, but it added a sense of fun throughout the storyline.<br /><br />The Unexpected Everything is wonderfully written with humour and charm, making it one of the loveliest young adult contemporaries this year. You know that feeling when you sleep in on a rainy Sunday morning. Cookies where the chocolate chips are still warm. When you spend a cold winters day reading and drinking tea or one of those bone crushing bear bugs to let you know you've been missed?<br /><br />The Unexpected Everything is that feeling and I adored each and every moment. And the dogs. Don't forget the dogs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7513422425625686954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nr7eqKYcpGgT12MZd/UVkZ4XwTG6x1zO9NJtSFB1RoQYqjPZqWmwaXeNQ1x8vlHQeYVsHondf0YO/6C1CIPH0g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kb6Za1iJrypm/Iye37FDWUKy+l0C5y6dawykv4U2IKqvqnQaV/y7KwKmrNvU+gcYpSBXcjH9DRWRIWlC3cCh/A==')})
  }

Megan’s not an actress, and she’s used to being upstaged—both in and out of the theater. In fact, with her mom off in Texas and her dad remarried and on to baby #2 with his new wife, Megan worries that, just like her exes, her family is moving on without her.\n\nThen she meets Owen Okita, an aspiring playwright inspired by Rosaline from Shakespeare\'s R+J. Yet Megan finds herself growing closer to Owen, and wonders if he could be the Romeo she never expected.\n\nIn their fresh and funny debut, Emily Wibberly and Austin Siegemund-Broka break down the       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson">About Morgan Matson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1281591801p3/3351454.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2237432942422488819">Morgan Matson grew up in New York City and Greenwich, Connecticut. She attended Occidental College in Los Angeles but halfway though a theater degree, she started working in the children's department of Vroman's Bookstore and fell in love with YA literature.<br/><br/>Following college graduation (and the proud bearer of an incredibly useful theater/English degree) she moved back East to attend the New Schoo</span>
  <span id="freeText2237432942422488819" style="display:none">Morgan Matson grew up in New York City and Greenwich, Connecticut. She attended Occidental College in Los Angeles but halfway though a theater degree, she started working in the children's department of Vroman's Bookstore and fell in love with YA literature.<br /><br />Following college graduation (and the proud bearer of an incredibly useful theater/English degree) she moved back East to attend the New School, where she received her M.F.A in Writing for Children.<br /><br />Amy &amp; Roger's Epic Detour, inspired by Morgan's three cross-country road trips, was published in May 2010. It was named an ALA Top Ten Best Book, a PW "Flying Start" book, and was shortlisted for the Waterstone's Book Prize.<br /><br />In the meantime, Morgan moved back to California, went back to school again and in 2011 received an M.F.A. in Screenwriting from the University of Southern California.<br /><br />Her second book, Second Chance Summer, was published in May 2012 and draws largely on her experiences spending summers growing up in the Pocono Mountains of Pennsylvania.<br /><br />Her third book, Since You've Been Gone, was published in 2014. <br /><br />Morgan currently lives in Los Angeles, though she loves to travel and does it whenever she can. She is currently writing another book, to be published in 2016.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2237432942422488819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
